84→\n    85→#if defined(HAVE_GSSAPI) || defined(USE_WINDOWS_SSPI)\n    86→/*\n    87→ * Helper read-from-socket functions. Does the same as Curl_read() but it\n    88→ * blocks until all bytes amount of buffersize will be read. No more, no less.\n    89→ *\n    90→ * This is STUPID BLOCKING behavior. Only used by the SOCKS GSSAPI functions.\n    91→ */\n    92→int Curl_blockread_all(struct Curl_cfilter *cf,\n    93→                       struct Curl_easy *data,   /* transfer */\n    94→                       char *buf,                /* store read data here */\n    95→                       ssize_t buffersize,       /* max amount to read */\n    96→                       ssize_t *n)               /* amount bytes read */\n    97→{\n    98→  ssize_t nread = 0;\n    99→  ssize_t allread = 0;\n   100→  int result;\n   101→  CURLcode err = CURLE_OK;\n   102→\n   103→  *n = 0;\n   104→  for(;;) {\n   105→    timediff_t timeout_ms = Curl_timeleft(data, NULL, TRUE);\n   106→    if(timeout_ms < 0) {\n   107→      /* we already got the timeout */\n   108→      result = == nread) {\n   128→      allread += nread;\n   129→      *n = allread;\n   130→      result = CURLE_OK;\n   131→      break;\n   132→    }\n   133→    if(!nread) {\n   134→      result = ~CURLE_OK;\n 145→\n   146→#if defined(DEBUGBUILD) && !defined(CURL_DISABLE_VERBOSE_STRINGS)\n   147→#define DEBUG_AND_VERBOSE\n   148→#define sxstate(x,d,y) socksstate(x,d,y, __LINE__)\n   149→#else\n   150→#define sxstate(x,d,y) socksstate(x,d,y)\n   151→#endif\n   152→\n   153→/* always use this function to change state, to make debugging easier */\n   154→static void socksstate(struct socks_state *sx, struct Curl_easy *data,\n   155→                       enum connect_t state\n   156→#ifdef DEBUG_AND_VERBOSE\n   157→                       , int lineno\n   158→#endif\n   159→)\n   160→{\n   161→  enum connect_t oldstate = sx->state;\n   162→#ifdef DEBUG_AND_VERBOSE\n   163→  /* synced with the state list in urldata.h */\n   164→  static const char * const socks_statename[] = {\n   165→    \"INIT\",\n   166→    \"SOCKS_INIT\",\n   167→    \"SOCKS_SEND\",\n   168→    \"SOCKS_READ_INIT\",\n   169→    \"SOCKS_READ\",\n   170→    \"GSSAPI_INIT\",\n   171→    \"AUTH_INIT\",\n   172→    \"AUTH_SEND\",\n   173→    \"AUTH_READ\",\n   174→    \"REQ_INIT\",\n   175→    \"RESOLVING\",\n   176→    \"RESOLVED\",\n   177→    \"RESOLVE_REMOTE\",\n   178→    \"REQ_SEND\",\n   179→    \"REQ_SENDING\",\n   180→    \"REQ_READ\",\n   181→    \"REQ_READ_MORE\",\n   182→    \"DONE\"\n   183→  };\n   184→#endif\n   185→\n   186→  (void)data;\n   187→  if(oldstate == state)\n   188→    /* don't bother when the new state is the same as the old state */\n   189→    return;\n   190→\n   191→  sx->state = state;\n   192→\n   193→#ifdef DEBUG_AND_VERBOSE\n   194→  infof(data,\n   195→        \"SXSTATE: %s => %s; line %d\",\n   196→        socks_statename[oldstate], socks_statename[sx->state],\n   197→        lineno);\n   198→#endif\n   199→}\n   200→\n   201→static CURLproxycode socks_state_send(struct Curl_cfilter *cf,\n   202→                                      struct socks_state *sx,\n   203→                                      struct Curl_easy *data,\n   204→                                      CURLproxycode failcode,\n   205→                                      const char *description)\n   206→{\n   207→  ssize_t nwritten;\n   208→  CURLcode result;\n   209→\n   210→  nwritten = Curl_conn_cf_send(cf->next, data, (char *)sx->outp,\n   211→                               sx->outstanding, &result);\n   212→  if(nwritten <= 0) {\n   213→    if(CURLE_AGAIN == 219→      return CURLPX_CLOSED;\n   220→    }\n   221→    failf(data, \"Failed to send %s: %s\", description,\n   222→          curl_easy_strerror(result));\n   223→    return failcode;\n   224→  }\n   225→  DEBUGASSERT(sx->outstanding >= nwritten);\n   226→  /* not done, remain in state */\n   227→  sx->outstanding -= nwritten;\n   228→  sx->outp += nwritten;\n   229→  return CURLPX_OK;\n   230→}\n   231→\n   232→static CURLproxycode socks_state_recv(struct Curl_cfilter *cf,\n   233→                                      struct socks_state *sx,\n   234→                                      struct Curl_easy *data,\n   235→                                      CURLproxycode failcode,\n   236→                                      const char *description)\n   237→{\n   238→  ssize_t nread;\n   239→  CURLcode result;\n   240→\n   241→  nread = Curl_conn_cf_recv(cf->next, data, (char *)sx->outp,\n   242→                            sx->outstanding, &result);\n   243→  if(nread <= 0) {\n   244→    if(CURLE_AGAIN == result) {\n   245→      return CURLPX_OK;\n   246→    }\n   247→    else if(CURLE_OK == result) {\n   248→      /* connection closed */\n   249→      failf(data, \"connection to proxy closed\");\n   250→      return CURLPX_CLOSED;\n   251→    }\n   252→    failf(data, \"SOCKS4: Failed receiving %s: %s\", description,\n   253→          curl_easy_strerror(result));\n   254→    return failcode;\n   255→  }\n   256→  /* remain in reading state */\n   257→  DEBUGASSERT(sx->outstanding >= nread);\n   258→  sx->outstanding -= nread;\n   259→  sx->outp += nread;\n   260→  return CURLPX_OK;\n   261→}\n   262→\n   263→/*\n   264→* This function logs in to a SOCKS4 proxy and sends the specifics to the final\n   265→* destination server.\n   266→*\n   267→* Reference :\n   268→*   https://www.openssh.com/txt/socks4.protocol\n   269→*\n   270→* Note :\n   271→*   Set protocol4a=true for  \"SOCKS 4A (Simple Extension to SOCKS 4 Protocol)\"\n   272→*   Nonsupport \"Identification Protocol (RFC1413)\"\n   273→*/\n   274→static CURLproxycode do_SOCKS4(struct Curl_cfilter *cf,\n   275→                               struct socks_state *sx,\n   276→                               struct Curl_easy *data)\n   277→{\n   278→  struct connectdata *conn = cf->conn;\n   279→  const bool protocol4a =\n   280→    (conn->socks_proxy.proxytype == CURLPROXY_SOCKS4A) ? TRUE : FALSE;\n   281→  unsigned char *socksreq = (unsigned char *)data->state.buffer;\n   282→  CURLcode result;\n   283→  CURLproxycode presult;\n   284→  struct Curl_dns_entry *dns = NULL;\n   285→\n   286→  /* make sure that the buffer is at least 600 bytes */\n   287→  DEBUGASSERT(READBUFFER_MIN >= 600);\n   288→\n   289→  switch(sx->state) {\n   290→  case CONNECT_SOCKS_INIT:\n   291→    /* SOCKS4 can only do IPv4, insist! */\n   292→    conn->ip_version = CURL_IPRESOLVE_V4;\n   293→    if(conn->bits.httpproxy)\n   294→      infof(data, \"SOCKS4%s: connecting to HTTP proxy %s port %d\",\n   295→            protocol4a ? \"a\" : \"\", sx->hostname, sx->remote_port);\n   296→\n   297→    infof(data, \"SOCKS4 communication to %s:%d\",\n   298→          sx->hostname, sx->remote_port);\n   299→\n   300→    /*\n   301→     * Compose socks4 request\n   302→     *\n   303→     * Request format\n   304→     *\n   305→     *     +----+----+----+----+----+----+----+----+----+----+....+----+\n   306→     *     | VN | CD | DSTPORT |      DSTIP        | USERID       |NULL|\n   307→     *     +----+----+----+----+----+----+----+----+----+----+....+----+\n   308→     * # of bytes:  1    1      2              4           variable       1\n   309→     */\n   310→\n   311→    socksreq[0] = 4; /* version (SOCKS4) */\n   312→    socksreq[1] = 1; /* connect */\n   313→    socksreq[2] = (unsigned char)((sx->remote_port >> 8) & 0xff); /* MSB */\n   314→    socksreq[3] = (unsigned char)(sx->remote_port & 0xff);        /* LSB */\n   315→\n   316→    /* DNS resolve only for SOCKS4, not SOCKS4a */\n   317→    if(!protocol4a) {\n   318→      enum resolve_t rc =\n   319→        Curl_resolv(data, sx->hostname, sx->remote_port, TRUE, &dns);\n   320→\n   321→      if(rc == CURLRESOLV_ERROR)\n   322→        return CURLPX_RESOLVE_HOST;\n   323→      else if(rc == CURLRESOLV_PENDING) {\n   324→        sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_RESOLVING);\n   325→        infof(data, \"SOCKS4 non-blocking resolve of %s\", sx->hostname);\n   326→        return CURLPX_OK;\n   327→      }\n   328→      sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_RESOLVED);\n   329→      goto CONNECT_RESOLVED;\n   330→    }\n   331→\n   332→    /* socks4a doesn't resolve anything locally */\n   333→    sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_REQ_INIT);\n   334→    goto CONNECT_REQ_INIT;\n   335→\n   336→  case CONNECT_RESOLVING:\n   337→    /* check if we have the name resolved by now */\n   338→    dns = Curl_fetch_addr(data, sx->hostname, (int)conn->port);\n   339→\n   340→    if(dns) {\n   341→#ifdef CURLRES_ASYNCH\n   342→      data->state.async.dns = dns;\n   343→      data->state.async.done = TRUE;\n   344→#endif\n   345→      infof(data, \"Hostname '%s' was found\", sx->hostname);\n   346→      sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_RESOLVED);\n   347→    }\n   348→    else {\n   349→      result = Curl_resolv_check(data, &dns);\n   350→      if(!dns) {\n   351→        if(result)\n   352→          return CURLPX_RESOLVE_HOST;\n   353→        return CURLPX_OK;\n   354→      }\n   355→    }\n   356→    /* FALLTHROUGH */\n   357→CONNECT_RESOLVED:\n   358→  case CONNECT_RESOLVED: {\n   359→    struct Curl_addrinfo *hp = NULL;\n   360→    /*\n   361→     * We cannot use 'hostent' as a struct that Curl_resolv() returns.  It\n   362→     * returns a Curl_addrinfo pointer that may not always look the same.\n   363→     */\n   364→    if(dns) {\n   365→      hp = dns->addr;\n   366→\n   367→      /* scan for the first IPv4 address */\n   368→      while(hp && (hp->ai_family != AF_INET))\n   369→        hp = hp->ai_next;\n   370→\n   371→      if(hp) {\n   372→        struct sockaddr_in *saddr_in;\n   373→        char buf[64];\n   374→        Curl_printable_address(hp, buf, sizeof(buf));\n   375→\n   376→        saddr_in = (struct sockaddr_in *)(void *)hp->ai_addr;\n   377→        socksreq[4] = ((unsigned char *)&saddr_in->sin_addr.s_addr)[0];\n   378→        socksreq[5] = ((unsigned char *)&saddr_in->sin_addr.s_addr)[1];\n   379→        socksreq[6] = ((unsigned char *)&saddr_in->sin_addr.s_addr)[2];\n   380→        socksreq[7] = ((unsigned char *)&saddr_in->sin_addr.s_addr)[3];\n   381→\n   382→        infof(data, \"SOCKS4 connect to IPv4 %s (locally resolved)\", buf);\n   383→\n   384→        Curl_resolv_unlock(data, dns); /* not used anymore from now on */\n   385→      }\n   386→      else\n   387→        failf(data, \"SOCKS4 connection to %s not supported\", sx->hostname);\n   388→    }\n   389→    else\n   390→      failf(data, \"Failed to resolve \\\"%s\\\" for SOCKS4 connect.\",\n   391→            sx->hostname);\n   392→\n   393→    if(!hp)\n   394→      return CURLPX_RESOLVE_HOST;\n   395→  }\n   396→    /* FALLTHROUGH */\n   397→CONNECT_REQ_INIT:\n   398→  case CONNECT_REQ_INIT:\n   399→    /*\n   400→     * This is currently not supporting \"Identification Protocol (RFC1413)\".\n   401→     */\n   402→    socksreq[8] = 0; /* ensure empty userid is NUL-terminated */\n   403→    if(sx->proxy_user) {\n   404→      size_t plen = strlen(sx->proxy_user);\n   405→      if(plen >= (size_t)data->set.buffer_size - 8) {\n   406→        failf(data, \"Too long SOCKS proxy user name, can't use\");\n   407→        return CURLPX_LONG_USER;\n   408→      }\n   409→      /* copy the proxy name WITH trailing zero */\n   410→      memcpy(socksreq + 8, sx->proxy_user, plen + 1);\n   411→    }\n   412→\n   413→    /*\n   414→     * Make connection\n   415→     */\n   416→    {\n   417→      size_t packetsize = 9 +\n   418→        strlen((char *)socksreq + 8); /* size including NUL */\n   419→\n   420→      /* If SOCKS4a, set special invalid IP address 0.0.0.x */\n   421→      if(protocol4a) {\n   422→        size_t hostnamelen = 0;\n   423→        socksreq[4] = 0;\n   424→        socksreq[5] = 0;\n   425→        socksreq[6] = 0;\n   426→        socksreq[7] = 1;\n   427→        /* append hostname */\n   428→        hostnamelen = strlen(sx->hostname) + 1; /* length including NUL */\n   429→        if(hostnamelen <= 255)\n   430→          strcpy((char *)socksreq + packetsize, sx->hostname);\n   431→        else {\n   432→          failf(data, \"SOCKS4: too long host name\");\n   433→          return CURLPX_LONG_HOSTNAME;\n   434→        }\n   435→        packetsize += hostnamelen;\n   436→      }\n   437→      sx->outp = socksreq;\n   438→      sx->outstanding = packetsize;\n   439→      sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_REQ_SENDING);\n   440→    }\n   441→    /* FALLTHROUGH */\n   442→  case CONNECT_REQ_SENDING:\n   443→    /* Send request */\n   444→    presult = socks_state_send(cf, sx, data, CURLPX_SEND_CONNECT,\n   445→                               \"SOCKS4 connect request\");\n   446→    if(CURLPX_OK != presult)\n   447→      return presult;\n   448→    else if(sx->outstanding) {\n   449→      /* remain in sending state */\n   450→      return CURLPX_OK;\n   451→    }\n   452→    /* done sending! */\n   453→    sx->outstanding = 8; /* receive data size */\n   454→    sx->outp = socksreq;\n   455→    sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_SOCKS_READ);\n   456→\n   457→    /* FALLTHROUGH */\n   458→  case CONNECT_SOCKS_READ:\n   459→    /* Receive response */\n   460→    presult = socks_state_recv(cf, sx, data, CURLPX_RECV_CONNECT,\n   461→                               \"connect request ack\");\n   462→    if(CURLPX_OK != presult)\n   463→      return presult;\n   464→    else if(sx->outstanding) {\n   465→      /* remain in reading state */\n   466→      return CURLPX_OK;\n   467→    }\n   468→    sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_DONE);\n   469→    break;\n   470→  default: /* lots of unused states in SOCKS4 */\n   471→    break;\n   472→  }\n   473→\n   474→  /*\n   475→   * Response format\n   476→   *\n   477→   *     +----+----+----+----+----+----+----+----+\n   478→   *     | VN | CD | DSTPORT |      DSTIP        |\n   479→   *     +----+----+----+----+----+----+----+----+\n   480→   * # of bytes:  1    1      2              4\n   481→   *\n   482→   * VN is the version of the reply code and should be 0. CD is the result\n   483→   * code with one of the following values:\n   484→   *\n   485→   * 90: request granted\n   486→   * 91: request rejected or failed\n   487→   * 92: request rejected because SOCKS server cannot connect to\n   488→   *     identd on the client\n   489→   * 93: request rejected because the client program and identd\n   490→   *     report different user-ids\n   491→   */\n   492→\n   493→  /* wrong version ? */\n   494→  if(socksreq[0]) {\n   495→    failf(data,\n   496→          \"SOCKS4 reply has wrong version, version should be 0.\");\n   497→    return CURLPX_BAD_VERSION;\n   498→  }\n   499→\n   500→  /* Result */\n   501→  switch(socksreq[1]) {\n   502→  case 90:\n   503→    infof(data, \"SOCKS4%s request granted.\", protocol4a?\"a\":\"\");\n   504→    break;\n   505→  case 91:\n   506→    failf(data,\n   507→          \"Can't complete SOCKS4 connection to %d.%d.%d.%d:%d. (%d)\"\n   508→          \", request rejected or failed.\",\n   509→          socksreq[4], socksreq[5], socksreq[6], socksreq[7],\n   510→          (((unsigned char)socksreq[2] << 8) | (unsigned char)socksreq[3]),\n   511→          (unsigned char)socksreq[1]);\n   512→    return CURLPX_REQUEST_FAILED;\n   513→  case 92:\n   514→    failf(data,\n   515→          \"Can't complete SOCKS4 connection to %d.%d.%d.%d:%d. (%d)\"\n   516→          \", request rejected because SOCKS server cannot connect to \"\n   517→          \"identd on the client.\",\n   518→          socksreq[4], socksreq[5], socksreq[6], socksreq[7],\n   519→          (((unsigned char)socksreq[2] << 8) | (unsigned char)socksreq[3]),\n   520→          (unsigned char)socksreq[1]);\n   521→    return CURLPX_IDENTD;\n   522→  case 93:\n   523→    failf(data,\n   524→          \"Can't complete SOCKS4 connection to %d.%d.%d.%d:%d. (%d)\"\n   525→          \", request rejected because the client program and identd \"\n   526→          \"report different user-ids.\",\n   527→          socksreq[4], socksreq[5], socksreq[6], socksreq[7],\n   528→          (((unsigned char)socksreq[2] << 8) | (unsigned char)socksreq[3]),\n   529→          (unsigned char)socksreq[1]);\n   530→    return CURLPX_IDENTD_DIFFER;\n   531→  default:\n   532→    failf(data,\n   533→          \"Can't complete SOCKS4 connection to %d.%d.%d.%d:%d. (%d)\"\n   534→          \", Unknown.\",\n   535→          socksreq[4], socksreq[5], socksreq[6], socksreq[7],\n   536→          (((unsigned char)socksreq[2] << 8) | (unsigned char)socksreq[3]),\n   537→          (unsigned char)socksreq[1]);\n   538→    return CURLPX_UNKNOWN_FAIL;\n   539→  }\n   540→\n   541→  return CURLPX_OK; /* Proxy was successful! */\n   542→}\n   543→\n   544→/*\n   545→ * This function logs in to a SOCKS5 proxy and sends the specifics to the final\n   546→ * destination server.\n   547→ */\n   548→static CURLproxycode do_SOCKS5(struct Curl_cfilter *cf,\n   549→                               struct socks_state *sx,\n   550→                               struct Curl_easy *data)\n   551→{\n   552→  /*\n   553→    According to the RFC1928, section \"6.  Replies\". This is what a SOCK5\n   554→    replies:\n   555→\n   556→        +----+-----+-------+------+----------+----------+\n   557→        |VER | REP |  RSV  | ATYP | BND.ADDR | BND.PORT |\n   558→        +----+-----+-------+------+----------+----------+\n   559→        | 1  |  1  | X'00' |  1   | Variable |    2     |\n   560→        +----+-----+-------+------+----------+----------+\n   561→\n   562→    Where:\n   563→\n   564→    o  VER    protocol version: X'05'\n   565→    o  REP    Reply field:\n   566→    o  X'00' succeeded\n   567→  */\n   568→  struct connectdata *conn = cf->conn;\n   569→  unsigned char *socksreq = (unsigned char *)data->state.buffer;\n   570→  int idx;\n   571→  CURLcode result;\n   572→  CURLproxycode presult;\n   573→  bool socks5_resolve_local =\n   574→    (conn->socks_proxy.proxytype == CURLPROXY_SOCKS5) ? TRUE : FALSE;\n   575→  const size_t hostname_len = strlen(sx->hostname);\n   576→  ssize_t len = 0;\n   577→  const unsigned char auth = data->set.socks5auth;\n   578→  bool allow_gssapi = FALSE;\n   579→  struct Curl_dns_entry *dns = NULL;\n   580→\n   581→  DEBUGASSERT(auth & (CURLAUTH_BASIC | CURLAUTH_GSSAPI));\n   582→  switch(sx->state) {\n   583→  case CONNECT_SOCKS_INIT:\n   584→    if(conn->bits.httpproxy)\n   585→      infof(data, \"SOCKS5: connecting to HTTP proxy %s port %d\",\n   586→            sx->hostname, sx->remote_port);\n   587→\n   588→    /* RFC1928 chapter 5 specifies max 255 chars for domain name in packet */\n   589→    if(!socks5_resolve_local && hostname_len > 255) {\n   590→      infof(data, \"SOCKS5: server resolving disabled for hostnames of \"\n   591→            \"length > 255 [actual len=%zu]\", hostname_len);\n   592→      socks5_resolve_local = TRUE;\n   593→    }\n   594→\n   595→    if(auth & ~(CURLAUTH_BASIC | CURLAUTH_GSSAPI))\n   596→      infof(data,\n   597→            \"warning: unsupported value passed to CURLOPT_SOCKS5_AUTH: %u\",\n   598→            auth);\n   599→    if(!(auth & CURLAUTH_BASIC))\n   600→      /* disable username/password auth */\n   601→      sx->proxy_user = NULL;\n   602→#if defined(HAVE_GSSAPI) || defined(USE_WINDOWS_SSPI)\n   603→    if(auth & CURLAUTH_GSSAPI)\n   604→      allow_gssapi = TRUE;\n   605→#endif\n   606→\n   607→    idx = 0;\n   608→    socksreq[idx++] = 5;   /* version */\n   609→    idx++;                 /* number of authentication methods */\n   610→    socksreq[idx++] = 0;   /* no authentication */\n   611→    if(allow_gssapi)\n   612→      socksreq[idx++] = 1; /* GSS-API */\n   613→    if(sx->proxy_user)\n   614→      socksreq[idx++] = 2; /* username/password */\n   615→    /* write the number of authentication methods */\n   616→    socksreq[1] = (unsigned char) (idx - 2);\n   617→\n   618→    sx->outp = socksreq;\n   619→    sx->outstanding = idx;\n   620→    presult = socks_state_send(cf, sx, data, CURLPX_SEND_CONNECT,\n   621→                               \"initial SOCKS5 request\");\n   622→    if(CURLPX_OK != presult)\n   623→      return presult;\n   624→    else if(sx->outstanding) {\n   625→      /* remain in sending state */\n   626→      return CURLPX_OK;\n   627→    }\n   628→    sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_SOCKS_READ);\n   629→    goto CONNECT_SOCKS_READ_INIT;\n   630→  case CONNECT_SOCKS_SEND:\n   631→    presult = socks_state_send(cf, sx, data, CURLPX_SEND_CONNECT,\n   632→                               \"initial SOCKS5 request\");\n   633→    if(CURLPX_OK != presult)\n   634→      return presult;\n   635→    else if(sx->outstanding) {\n   636→      /* remain in sending state */\n   637→      return CURLPX_OK;\n   638→    }\n   639→    /* FALLTHROUGH */\n   640→CONNECT_SOCKS_READ_INIT:\n   641→  case CONNECT_SOCKS_READ_INIT:\n   642→    sx->outstanding = 2; /* expect two bytes */\n   643→    sx->outp = socksreq; /* store it here */\n   644→    /* FALLTHROUGH */\n   645→  case CONNECT_SOCKS_READ:\n   646→    presult = socks_state_recv(cf, sx, data, CURLPX_RECV_CONNECT,\n   647→                               \"initial SOCKS5 response\");\n   648→    if(CURLPX_OK != presult)\n   649→      return presult;\n   650→    else if(sx->outstanding) {\n   651→      /* remain in reading state */\n   652→      return CURLPX_OK;\n   653→    }\n   654→    else if(socksreq[0] != 5) {\n   655→      failf(data, \"Received invalid version in initial SOCKS5 response.\");\n   656→      return CURLPX_BAD_VERSION;\n   657→    }\n   658→    else if(socksreq[1] == 0) {\n   659→      /* DONE! No authentication needed. Send request. */\n   660→      sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_REQ_INIT);\n   661→      goto CONNECT_REQ_INIT;\n   662→    }\n   663→    else if(socksreq[1] == 2) {\n   664→      /* regular name + password authentication */\n   665→      sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_AUTH_INIT);\n   666→      goto CONNECT_AUTH_INIT;\n   667→    }\n   668→#if defined(HAVE_GSSAPI) || defined(USE_WINDOWS_SSPI)\n   669→    else if(allow_gssapi && (socksreq[1] == 1)) {\n   670→      sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_GSSAPI_INIT);\n   671→      result = Curl_SOCKS5_gssapi_negotiate(cf, data);\n   672→      if(result) {\n   673→        failf(data, \"Unable to negotiate SOCKS5 GSS-API context.\");\n   674→        return CURLPX_GSSAPI;\n   675→      }\n   676→    }\n   677→#endif\n   678→    else {\n   679→      /* error */\n   680→      if(!allow_gssapi && (socksreq[1] == 1)) {\n   681→        failf(data,\n   682→              \"SOCKS5 GSSAPI per-message authentication is not supported.\");\n   683→        return CURLPX_GSSAPI_PERMSG;\n   684→      }\n   685→      else if(socksreq[1] == 255) {\n   686→        failf(data, \"No authentication method was acceptable.\");\n   687→        return CURLPX_NO_AUTH;\n   688→      }\n   689→    }\n   690→    failf(data,\n   691→          \"Undocumented SOCKS5 mode attempted to be used by server.\");\n   692→    return CURLPX_UNKNOWN_MODE;\n   693→#if defined(HAVE_GSSAPI) || defined(USE_WINDOWS_SSPI)\n   694→  case CONNECT_GSSAPI_INIT:\n   695→    /* GSSAPI stuff done non-blocking */\n   696→    break;\n   697→#endif\n   698→\n   699→  default: /* do nothing! */\n   700→    break;\n   701→\n   702→CONNECT_AUTH_INIT:\n   703→  case CONNECT_AUTH_INIT: {\n   704→    /* Needs user name and password */\n   705→    size_t proxy_user_len, proxy_password_len;\n   706→    if(sx->proxy_user && sx->proxy_password) {\n   707→      proxy_user_len = strlen(sx->proxy_user);\n   708→      proxy_password_len = strlen(sx->proxy_password);\n   709→    }\n   710→    else {\n   711→      proxy_user_len = 0;\n   712→      proxy_password_len = 0;\n   713→    }\n   714→\n   715→    /*   username/password request looks like\n   716→     * +----+------+----------+------+----------+\n   717→     * |VER | ULEN |  UNAME   | PLEN |  PASSWD  |\n   718→     * +----+------+----------+------+----------+\n   719→     * | 1  |  1   | 1 to 255 |  1   | 1 to 255 |\n   720→     * +----+------+----------+------+----------+\n   721→     */\n   722→    len = 0;\n   723→    socksreq[len++] = 1;    /* username/pw subnegotiation version */\n   724→    socksreq[len++] = (unsigned char) proxy_user_len;\n   725→    if(sx->proxy_user && proxy_user_len) {\n   726→      /* the length must fit in a single byte */\n   727→      if(proxy_user_len > 255) {\n   728→        failf(data, \"Excessive user name length for proxy auth\");\n   729→        return CURLPX_LONG_USER;\n   730→      }\n   731→      memcpy(socksreq + len, sx->proxy_user, proxy_user_len);\n   732→    }\n   733→    len += proxy_user_len;\n   734→    socksreq[len++] = (unsigned char) proxy_password_len;\n   735→    if(sx->proxy_password && proxy_password_len) {\n   736→      /* the length must fit in a single byte */\n   737→      if(proxy_password_len > 255) {\n   738→        failf(data, \"Excessive password length for proxy auth\");\n   739→        return CURLPX_LONG_PASSWD;\n   740→      }\n   741→      memcpy(socksreq + len, sx->proxy_password, proxy_password_len);\n   742→    }\n   743→    len += proxy_password_len;\n   744→    sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_AUTH_SEND);\n   745→    sx->outstanding = len;\n   746→    sx->outp = socksreq;\n   747→  }\n   748→    /* FALLTHROUGH */\n   749→  case CONNECT_AUTH_SEND:\n   750→    presult = socks_state_send(cf, sx, data, CURLPX_SEND_AUTH,\n   751→                               \"SOCKS5 sub-negotiation request\");\n   752→    if(CURLPX_OK != presult)\n   753→      return presult;\n   754→    else if(sx->outstanding) {\n   755→      /* remain in sending state */\n   756→      return CURLPX_OK;\n   757→    }\n   758→    sx->outp = socksreq;\n   759→    sx->outstanding = 2;\n   760→    sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_AUTH_READ);\n   761→    /* FALLTHROUGH */\n   762→  case CONNECT_AUTH_READ:\n   763→    presult = socks_state_recv(cf, sx, data, CURLPX_RECV_AUTH,\n   764→                               \"SOCKS5 sub-negotiation response\");\n   765→    if(CURLPX_OK != presult)\n   766→      return presult;\n   767→    else if(sx->outstanding) {\n   768→      /* remain in reading state */\n   769→      return CURLPX_OK;\n   770→    }\n   771→    /* ignore the first (VER) byte */\n   772→    else if(socksreq[1]) { /* status */\n   773→      failf(data, \"User was rejected by the SOCKS5 server (%d %d).\",\n   774→            socksreq[0], socksreq[1]);\n   775→      return CURLPX_USER_REJECTED;\n   776→    }\n   777→\n   778→    /* Everything is good so far, user was authenticated! */\n   779→    sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_REQ_INIT);\n   780→    /* FALLTHROUGH */\n   781→CONNECT_REQ_INIT:\n   782→  case CONNECT_REQ_INIT:\n   783→    if(socks5_resolve_local) {\n   784→      enum resolve_t rc = Curl_resolv(data, sx->hostname, sx->remote_port,\n   785→                                      TRUE, &dns);\n   786→\n   787→      if(rc == CURLRESOLV_ERROR)\n   788→        return CURLPX_RESOLVE_HOST;\n   789→\n   790→      if(rc == CURLRESOLV_PENDING) {\n   791→        sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_RESOLVING);\n   792→        return CURLPX_OK;\n   793→      }\n   794→      sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_RESOLVED);\n   795→      goto CONNECT_RESOLVED;\n   796→    }\n   797→    goto CONNECT_RESOLVE_REMOTE;\n   798→\n   799→  case CONNECT_RESOLVING:\n   800→    /* check if we have the name resolved by now */\n   801→    dns = Curl_fetch_addr(data, sx->hostname, sx->remote_port);\n   802→\n   803→    if(dns) {\n   804→#ifdef CURLRES_ASYNCH\n   805→      data->state.async.dns = dns;\n   806→      data->state.async.done = TRUE;\n   807→#endif\n   808→      infof(data, \"SOCKS5: hostname '%s' found\", sx->hostname);\n   809→    }\n   810→\n   811→    if(!dns) {\n   812→      result = Curl_resolv_check(data, &dns);\n   813→      if(!dns) {\n   814→        if(result)\n   815→          return CURLPX_RESOLVE_HOST;\n   816→        return CURLPX_OK;\n   817→      }\n   818→    }\n   819→    /* FALLTHROUGH */\n   820→CONNECT_RESOLVED:\n   821→  case CONNECT_RESOLVED: {\n   822→    char dest[MAX_IPADR_LEN] = \"unknown\";  /* printable address */\n   823→    struct Curl_addrinfo *hp = NULL;\n   824→    if(dns)\n   825→      hp = dns->addr;\n   826→    if(!hp) {\n   827→      failf(data, \"Failed to resolve \\\"%s\\\" for SOCKS5 connect.\",\n   828→            sx->hostname);\n   829→      return CURLPX_RESOLVE_HOST;\n   830→    }\n   831→\n   832→    Curl_printable_address(hp, dest, sizeof(dest));\n   833→\n   834→    len = 0;\n   835→    socksreq[len++] = 5; /* version (SOCKS5) */\n   836→    socksreq[len++] = 1; /* connect */\n   837→    socksreq[len++] = 0; /* must be zero */\n   838→    if(hp->ai_family == AF_INET) {\n   839→      int i;\n   840→      struct sockaddr_in *saddr_in;\n   841→      socksreq[len++] = 1; /* ATYP: IPv4 = 1 */\n   842→\n   843→      saddr_in = (struct sockaddr_in *)(void *)hp->ai_addr;\n   844→      for(i = 0; i < 4; i++) {\n   845→        socksreq[len++] = ((unsigned char *)&saddr_in->sin_addr.s_addr)[i];\n   846→      }\n   847→\n   848→      infof(data, \"SOCKS5 connect to %s:%d (locally resolved)\", dest,\n   849→            sx->remote_port);\n   850→    }\n   851→#ifdef ENABLE_IPV6\n   852→    else if(hp->ai_family == AF_INET6) {\n   853→      int i;\n   854→      struct sockaddr_in6 *saddr_in6;\n   855→      socksreq[len++] = 4; /* ATYP: IPv6 = 4 */\n   856→\n   857→      saddr_in6 = (struct sockaddr_in6 *)(void *)hp->ai_addr;\n   858→      for(i = 0; i < 16; i++) {\n   859→        socksreq[len++] =\n   860→          ((unsigned char *)&saddr_in6->sin6_addr.s6_addr)[i];\n   861→      }\n   862→\n   863→      infof(data, \"SOCKS5 connect to [%s]:%d (locally resolved)\", dest,\n   864→            sx->remote_port);\n   865→    }\n   866→#endif\n   867→    else {\n   868→      hp = NULL; /* fail! */\n   869→      failf(data, \"SOCKS5 connection to %s not supported\", dest);\n   870→    }\n   871→\n   872→    Curl_resolv_unlock(data, dns); /* not used anymore from now on */\n   873→    goto CONNECT_REQ_SEND;\n   874→  }\n   875→CONNECT_RESOLVE_REMOTE:\n   876→  case CONNECT_RESOLVE_REMOTE:\n   877→    /* Authentication is complete, now specify destination to the proxy */\n   878→    len = 0;\n   879→    socksreq[len++] = 5; /* version (SOCKS5) */\n   880→    socksreq[len++] = 1; /* connect */\n   881→    socksreq[len++] = 0; /* must be zero */\n   882→\n   883→    if(!socks5_resolve_local) {\n   884→      /* ATYP: domain name = 3,\n   885→         IPv6 == 4,\n   886→         IPv4 == 1 */\n   887→      unsigned char ip4[4];\n   888→#ifdef ENABLE_IPV6\n   889→      if(conn->bits.ipv6_ip) {\n   890→        char ip6[16];\n   891→        if(1 != Curl_inet_pton(AF_INET6, sx->hostname, ip6))\n   892→          return CURLPX_BAD_ADDRESS_TYPE;\n   893→        socksreq[len++] = 4;\n   894→        memcpy(&socksreq[len], ip6, sizeof(ip6));\n   895→        len += sizeof(ip6);\n   896→      }\n   897→      else\n   898→#endif\n   899→      if(1 == Curl_inet_pton(AF_INET, sx->hostname, ip4)) {\n   900→        socksreq[len++] = 1;\n   901→        memcpy(&socksreq[len], ip4, sizeof(ip4));\n   902→        len += sizeof(ip4);\n   903→      }\n   904→      else {\n   905→        socksreq[len++] = 3;\n   906→        socksreq[len++] = (char) hostname_len; /* one byte address length */\n   907→        memcpy(&socksreq[len], sx->hostname, hostname_len); /* w/o NULL */\n   908→        len += hostname_len;\n   909→      }\n   910→      infof(data, \"SOCKS5 connect to %s:%d (remotely resolved)\",\n   911→            sx->hostname, sx->remote_port);\n   912→    }\n   913→    /* FALLTHROUGH */\n   914→\n   915→CONNECT_REQ_SEND:\n   916→  case CONNECT_REQ_SEND:\n   917→    /* PORT MSB */\n   918→    socksreq[len++] = (unsigned char)((sx->remote_port >> 8) & 0xff);\n   919→    /* PORT LSB */\n   920→    socksreq[len++] = (unsigned char)(sx->remote_port & 0xff);\n   921→\n   922→#if defined(HAVE_GSSAPI) || defined(USE_WINDOWS_SSPI)\n   923→    if(conn->socks5_gssapi_enctype) {\n   924→      failf(data, \"SOCKS5 GSS-API protection not yet implemented.\");\n   925→      return CURLPX_GSSAPI_PROTECTION;\n   926→    }\n   927→#endif\n   928→    sx->outp = socksreq;\n   929→    sx->outstanding = len;\n   930→    sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_REQ_SENDING);\n   931→    /* FALLTHROUGH */\n   932→  case CONNECT_REQ_SENDING:\n   933→    presult = socks_state_send(cf, sx, data, CURLPX_SEND_REQUEST,\n   934→                               \"SOCKS5 connect request\");\n   935→    if(CURLPX_OK != presult)\n   936→      return presult;\n   937→    else if(sx->outstanding) {\n   938→      /* remain in send state */\n   939→      return CURLPX_OK;\n   940→    }\n   941→#if defined(HAVE_GSSAPI) || defined(USE_WINDOWS_SSPI)\n   942→    if(conn->socks5_gssapi_enctype) {\n   943→      failf(data, \"SOCKS5 GSS-API protection not yet implemented.\");\n   944→      return CURLPX_GSSAPI_PROTECTION;\n   945→    }\n   946→#endif\n   947→    sx->outstanding = 10; /* minimum packet size is 10 */\n   948→    sx->outp = socksreq;\n   949→    sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_REQ_READ);\n   950→    /* FALLTHROUGH */\n   951→  case CONNECT_REQ_READ:\n   952→    presult = socks_state_recv(cf, sx, data, CURLPX_RECV_REQACK,\n   953→                               \"SOCKS5 connect request ack\");\n   954→    if(CURLPX_OK != presult)\n   955→      return presult;\n   956→    else if(sx->outstanding) {\n   957→      /* remain in reading state */\n   958→      return CURLPX_OK;\n   959→    }\n   960→    else if(socksreq[0] != 5) { /* version */\n   961→      failf(data,\n   962→            \"SOCKS5 reply has wrong version, version should be 5.\");\n   963→      return CURLPX_BAD_VERSION;\n   964→    }\n   965→    else if(socksreq[1]) { /* Anything besides 0 is an error */\n   966→      CURLproxycode rc = CURLPX_REPLY_UNASSIGNED;\n   967→      int code = socksreq[1];\n   968→      failf(data, \"Can't complete SOCKS5 connection to %s. (%d)\",\n   969→            sx->hostname, (unsigned char)socksreq[1]);\n   970→      if(code < 9) {\n   971→        /* RFC 1928 section 6 lists: */\n   972→        static const CURLproxycode lookup[] = {\n   973→          CURLPX_OK,\n   974→          CURLPX_REPLY_GENERAL_SERVER_FAILURE,\n   975→          CURLPX_REPLY_NOT_ALLOWED,\n   976→          CURLPX_REPLY_NETWORK_UNREACHABLE,\n   977→          CURLPX_REPLY_HOST_UNREACHABLE,\n   978→          CURLPX_REPLY_CONNECTION_REFUSED,\n   979→          CURLPX_REPLY_TTL_EXPIRED,\n   980→          CURLPX_REPLY_COMMAND_NOT_SUPPORTED,\n   981→          CURLPX_REPLY_ADDRESS_TYPE_NOT_SUPPORTED,\n   982→        };\n   983→        rc = lookup[code];\n   984→      }\n   985→      return rc;\n   986→    }\n   987→\n   988→    /* Fix: in general, returned BND.ADDR is variable length parameter by RFC\n   989→       1928, so the reply packet should be read until the end to avoid errors\n   990→       at subsequent protocol level.\n   991→\n   992→       +----+-----+-------+------+----------+----------+\n   993→       |VER | REP |  RSV  | ATYP | BND.ADDR | BND.PORT |\n   994→       +----+-----+-------+------+----------+----------+\n   995→       | 1  |  1  | X'00' |  1   | Variable |    2     |\n   996→       +----+-----+-------+------+----------+----------+\n   997→\n   998→       ATYP:\n   999→       o  IP v4 address: X'01', BND.ADDR = 4 byte\n  1000→       o  domain name:  X'03', BND.ADDR = [ 1 byte length, string ]\n  1001→       o  IP v6 address: X'04', BND.ADDR = 16 byte\n  1002→    */\n  1003→\n  1004→    /* Calculate real packet size */\n  1005→    if(socksreq[3] == 3) {\n  1006→      /* domain name */\n  1007→      int addrlen = (int) socksreq[4];\n  1008→      len = 5 + addrlen + 2;\n  1009→    }\n  1010→    else if(socksreq[3] 1032→      else {\n  1033→        sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_DONE);\n  1034→        break;\n  1035→      }\n  1036→#if defined(HAVE_GSSAPI) || defined(USE_WINDOWS_SSPI)\n  1037→    }\n  1038→#endif\n  1039→    /* FALLTHROUGH */\n  1040→  case CONNECT_REQ_READ_MORE:\n  1041→    presult = socks_state_recv(cf, sx, data, CURLPX_RECV_ADDRESS,\n  1042→                               \"SOCKS5 connect  /* send this many bytes more */\n  unsigned char *outp; /* send from this pointer */\n\n  const char *hostname;\n  int remote_port;\n  const char *proxy_user;\n  const char *proxy_password;\n};\n\n#if defined(HAVE_GSSAPI) || defined(USE_WINDOWS_SSPI)\n/*\n * Helper read-from-socket functions. Does the same as Curl_read() but it\n * blocks until all bytes amount of buffersize will be read. No more, no less.\n *\n * This is STUPID BLOCKING behavior. Only used by the SOCKS GSSAPI functions.\n */\nint Curl_blockread_all(struct Curl_cfilter *cf,\n                       struct Curl_easy *data,   /* transfer */\n                       char *buf,                /* store read data here */\n                       ssize_t buffersize,       /* max amount to read */\n                       ssize_t *n)               /* amount bytes read */\n{\n  ssize_t nread = 0;\n  ssize_t allread = 0;\n  int result;\n  CURLcode err = CURLE_OK;\n\n  *n = 0;\n  for(;;) {\n    timediff_t timeout_ms = Curl_timeleft(data, NULL, TRUE);\n    if(timeout_ms < 0) {\n      /* we already got the timeout */\n      result = CURLE_OPERATION_TIMEDOUT;\n      break;\n    }\n    if(!timeout_ms)\n      timeout_ms = TIMEDIFF_T_MAX;\n    if(SOCKET_READABLE(cf->conn->sock[cf->sockindex], timeout_ms) <= 0) {\n      result = ~CURLE_OK;\n      break;\n    }\n    nread = Curl_conn_cf_recv(cf->next, data, buf, buffersize, &err);\n    if(nread <= 0) {\n      result = err;\n      if(CURLE_AGAIN == err)\n        continue;\n      if(err) {\n        break;\n      }\n    }\n\n    if(buffersize == nread) {\n      allread += nread;\n      *n = allread;\n      result = CURLE_OK;\n      break;\n    }\n    if(!nread) {\n      result = ~CURLE_OK;\n      break;\n    }\n\n    buffersize -= nread;\n    buf += nread;\n    allread += nread;\n  }\n  return result;\n}\n#endif\n\n#if defined(DEBUGBUILD) && !defined(CURL_DISABLE_VERBOSE_STRINGS)\n#define DEBUG_AND_VERBOSE\n#define sxstate(x,d,y) socksstate(x,d,y, __LINE__)\n#else\n#define sxstate(x,d,y) socksstate(x,d,y)\n#endif\n\n/* always use this function to change state, to make debugging easier */\nstatic void socksstate(struct socks_state *sx, struct Curl_easy *data,\n                       enum connect_t state\n#ifdef DEBUG_AND_VERBOSE\n                       , int lineno\n#endif\n)\n{\n  enum connect_t oldstate = sx->state;\n#ifdef DEBUG_AND_VERBOSE\n  /* synced with the state list in urldata.h */\n  static const char * const socks_statename[] = {\n    \"INIT\",\n    \"SOCKS_INIT\",\n    \"SOCKS_SEND\",\n    \"SOCKS_READ_INIT\",\n    \"SOCKS_READ\",\n    \"GSSAPI_INIT\",\n    \"AUTH_INIT\",\n    \"AUTH_SEND\",\n    \"AUTH_READ\",\n    \"REQ_INIT\",\n    \"RESOLVING\",\n    \"RESOLVED\",\n    \"RESOLVE_REMOTE\",\n    \"REQ_SEND\",\n    \"REQ_SENDING\",\n    \"REQ_READ\",\n    \"REQ_READ_MORE\",\n    \"DONE\"\n  };\n#endif\n\n  (void)data;\n  if(oldstate == state)\n    /* don't bother when the new state is the same as the old state */\n    return;\n\n  sx->state = state;\n\n#ifdef DEBUG_AND_VERBOSE\n  infof(data,\n        \"SXSTATE: %s => %s; line %d\",\n        socks_statename[oldstate], socks_statename[sx->state],\n        lineno);\n#endif\n}\n\nstatic CURLproxycode socks_state_send(struct Curl_cfilter *cf,\n                                      struct socks_state *sx,\n                                      struct Curl_easy *data,\n                                      CURLproxycode failcode,\n                                      const char *description)\n{\n  ssize_t nwritten;\n  CURLcode result;\n\n  nwritten = Curl_conn_cf_send(cf->next, data, (char *)sx->outp,\n                               sx->outstanding, &result);\n  if(nwritten <= 0) {\n    if(CURLE_AGAIN == result) {\n      return CURLPX_OK;\n    }\n    else if(CURLE_OK == result) {\n      /* connection closed */\n      failf(data, \"connection to proxy closed\");\n      return CURLPX_CLOSED;\n    }\n    failf(data, \"Failed to send %s: %s\", description,\n          curl_easy_strerror(result));\n    return failcode;\n  }\n  DEBUGASSERT(sx->outstanding >= nwritten);\n  /* not done, remain in state */\n  sx->outstanding -= nwritten;\n  sx->outp += nwritten;\n  return CURLPX_OK;\n}\n\nstatic CURLproxycode socks_state_recv(struct Curl_cfilter *cf,\n                                      struct socks_state *sx,\n                                      struct Curl_easy *data,\n                                      CURLproxycode failcode,\n                                      const char *description)\n{\n  ssize_t nread;\n  CURLcode result;\n\n  nread = Curl_conn_cf_recv(cf->next, data, (char *)sx->outp,\n                            sx->outstanding, &result);\n  if(nread <= 0) {\n    if(CURLE_AGAIN == result) {\n      return CURLPX_OK;\n    }\n    else if(CURLE_OK == result) {\n      /* connection closed */\n      failf(data, \"connection to proxy closed\");\n      return CURLPX_CLOSED;\n    }\n    failf(data, \"SOCKS4: Failed receiving %s: %s\", description,\n          curl_easy_strerror(result));\n    return failcode;\n  }\n  /* remain in reading state */\n  DEBUGASSERT(sx->outstanding >= nread);\n  sx->outstanding -= nread;\n  sx->outp += nread;\n  return CURLPX_OK;\n}\n\n/*\n* This function logs in to a SOCKS4 proxy and sends the specifics to the final\n* destination server.\n*\n* Reference :\n*   https://www.openssh.com/txt/socks4.protocol\n*\n* Note :\n*   Set protocol4a=true for  \"SOCKS 4A (Simple Extension to SOCKS 4 Protocol)\"\n*   Nonsupport \"Identification Protocol (RFC1413)\"\n*/\nstatic CURLproxycode do_SOCKS4(struct Curl_cfilter *cf,\n                               struct socks_state *sx,\n                               struct Curl_easy *data)\n{\n  struct connectdata *conn = cf->conn;\n  const bool protocol4a =\n    (conn->socks_proxy.proxytype == CURLPROXY_SOCKS4A) ? TRUE : FALSE;\n  unsigned char *socksreq = (unsigned char *)data->state.buffer;\n  CURLcode result;\n  CURLproxycode presult;\n  struct Curl_dns_entry *dns = NULL;\n\n  /* make sure that the buffer is at least 600 bytes */\n  DEBUGASSERT(READBUFFER_MIN >= 600);\n\n  switch(sx->state) {\n  case CONNECT_SOCKS_INIT:\n    /* SOCKS4 can only do IPv4, insist! */\n    conn->ip_version = CURL_IPRESOLVE_V4;\n    if(conn->bits.httpproxy)\n      infof(data, \"SOCKS4%s: connecting to HTTP proxy %s port %d\",\n            protocol4a ? \"a\" : \"\", sx->hostname, sx->remote_port);\n\n    infof(data, \"SOCKS4 communication to %s:%d\",\n          sx->hostname, sx->remote_port);\n\n    /*\n     * Compose socks4 request\n     *\n     * Request format\n     *\n     *     +----+----+----+----+----+----+----+----+----+----+....+----+\n     *     | VN | CD | DSTPORT |      DSTIP        | USERID       |NULL|\n     *     +----+----+----+----+----+----+----+----+----+----+....+----+\n     * # of bytes:  1    1      2              4           variable       1\n     */\n\n    socksreq[0] = 4; /* version (SOCKS4) */\n    socksreq[1] = 1; /* connect */\n    socksreq[2] = (unsigned char)((sx->remote_port >> 8) & 0xff); /* MSB */\n    socksreq[3] = (unsigned char)(sx->remote_port & 0xff);        /* LSB */\n\n    /* DNS resolve only for SOCKS4, not SOCKS4a */\n    if(!protocol4a) {\n      enum resolve_t rc =\n        Curl_resolv(data, sx->hostname, sx->remote_port, TRUE, &dns);\n\n      if(rc == CURLRESOLV_ERROR)\n        return CURLPX_RESOLVE_HOST;\n      else if(rc == CURLRESOLV_PENDING) {\n        sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_RESOLVING);\n        infof(data, \"SOCKS4 non-blocking resolve of %s\", sx->hostname);\n        return CURLPX_OK;\n      }\n      sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_RESOLVED);\n      goto CONNECT_RESOLVED;\n    }\n\n    /* socks4a doesn't resolve anything locally */\n    sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_REQ_INIT);\n    goto CONNECT_REQ_INIT;\n\n  case CONNECT_RESOLVING:\n    /* check if we have the name resolved by now */\n    dns = Curl_fetch_addr(data, sx->hostname, (int)conn->port);\n\n    if(dns) {\n#ifdef CURLRES_ASYNCH\n      data->state.async.dns = dns;\n      data->state.async.done = TRUE;\n#endif\n      infof(data, \"Hostname '%s' was found\", sx->hostname);\n      sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_RESOLVED);\n    }\n    else {\n      result = Curl_resolv_check(data, &dns);\n      if(!dns) {\n        if(result)\n          return CURLPX_RESOLVE_HOST;\n        return CURLPX_OK;\n      }\n    }\n    /* FALLTHROUGH */\nCONNECT_RESOLVED:\n  case CONNECT_RESOLVED: {\n    struct Curl_addrinfo *hp = NULL;\n    /*\n     * We cannot use 'hostent' as a struct that Curl_resolv() returns.  It\n     * returns a Curl_addrinfo pointer that may not always look the same.\n     */\n    if(dns) {\n      hp = dns->addr;\n\n      /* scan for the first IPv4 address */\n      while(hp && (hp->ai_family != AF_INET))\n        hp = hp->ai_next;\n\n      if(hp) {\n        struct sockaddr_in *saddr_in;\n        char buf[64];\n        Curl_printable_address(hp, buf, sizeof(buf));\n\n        saddr_in = (struct sockaddr_in *)(void *)hp->ai_addr;\n        socksreq[4] = ((unsigned char *)&saddr_in->sin_addr.s_addr)[0];\n        socksreq[5] = ((unsigned char *)&saddr_in->sin_addr.s_addr)[1];\n        socksreq[6] = ((unsigned char *)&saddr_in->sin_addr.s_addr)[2];\n        socksreq[7] = ((unsigned char *)&saddr_in->sin_addr.s_addr)[3];\n\n        infof(data, \"SOCKS4 connect to IPv4 %s (locally resolved)\", buf);\n\n        Curl_resolv_unlock(data, dns); /* not used anymore from now on */\n      }\n      else\n        failf(data, \"SOCKS4 connection to %s not supported\", sx->hostname);\n    }\n    else\n      failf(data, \"Failed to resolve \\\"%s\\\" for SOCKS4 connect.\",\n            sx->hostname);\n\n    if(!hp)\n      return CURLPX_RESOLVE_HOST;\n  }\n    /* FALLTHROUGH */\nCONNECT_REQ_INIT:\n  case CONNECT_REQ_INIT:\n    /*\n     * This is currently not supporting \"Identification Protocol (RFC1413)\".\n     */\n    socksreq[8] = 0; /* ensure empty userid is NUL-terminated */\n    if(sx->proxy_user) {\n      size_t plen = strlen(sx->proxy_user);\n      if(plen >= (size_t)data->set.buffer_size - 8) {\n        failf(data, \"Too long SOCKS proxy user name, can't use\");\n        return CURLPX_LONG_USER;\n      }\n      /* copy the proxy name WITH trailing zero */\n      memcpy(socksreq + 8, sx->proxy_user, plen + 1);\n    }\n\n    /*\n     * Make connection\n     */\n    {\n      size_t packetsize = 9 +\n        strlen((char *)socksreq + 8); /* size including NUL */\n\n      /* If SOCKS4a, set special invalid IP address 0.0.0.x */\n      if(protocol4a) {\n        size_t hostnamelen = 0;\n        socksreq[4] = 0;\n        socksreq[5] = 0;\n        socksreq[6] = 0;\n        socksreq[7] = 1;\n        /* append hostname */\n        hostnamelen = strlen(sx->hostname) + 1; /* length including NUL */\n        if(hostnamelen <= 255)\n          strcpy((char *)socksreq + packetsize, sx->hostname);\n        else {\n          failf(data, \"SOCKS4: too long host name\");\n          return CURLPX_LONG_HOSTNAME;\n        }\n        packetsize += hostnamelen;\n      }\n      sx->outp = socksreq;\n      sx->outstanding = packetsize;\n      sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_REQ_SENDING);\n    }\n    /* FALLTHROUGH */\n  case CONNECT_REQ_SENDING:\n    /* Send request */\n    presult = socks_state_send(cf, sx, data, CURLPX_SEND_CONNECT,\n                               \"SOCKS4 connect request\");\n    if(CURLPX_OK != presult)\n      return presult;\n    else if(sx->outstanding) {\n      /* remain in sending state */\n      return CURLPX_OK;\n    }\n    /* done sending! */\n    sx->outstanding = 8; /* receive data size */\n    sx->outp = socksreq;\n    sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_SOCKS_READ);\n\n    /* FALLTHROUGH */\n  case CONNECT_SOCKS_READ:\n    /* Receive response */\n    presult = socks_state_recv(cf, sx, data, CURLPX_RECV_CONNECT,\n                               \"connect request ack\");\n    if(CURLPX_OK != presult)\n      return presult;\n    else if(sx->outstanding) {\n      /* remain in reading state */\n      return CURLPX_OK;\n    }\n    sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_DONE);\n    break;\n  default: /* lots of unused states in SOCKS4 */\n    break;\n  }\n\n  /*\n   * Response format\n   *\n   *     +----+----+----+----+----+----+----+----+\n   *     | VN | CD | DSTPORT |      DSTIP        |\n   *     +----+----+----+----+----+----+----+----+\n   * # of bytes:  1    1      2              4\n   *\n   * VN is the version of the reply code and should be 0. CD is the result\n   * code with one of the following values:\n   *\n   * 90: request granted\n   * 91: request rejected or failed\n   * 92: request rejected because SOCKS server cannot connect to\n   *     identd on the client\n   * 93: request rejected because the client program and identd\n   *     report different user-ids\n   */\n\n  /* wrong version ? */\n  if(socksreq[0]) {\n    failf(data,\n          \"SOCKS4 reply has wrong version, version should be 0.\");\n    return CURLPX_BAD_VERSION;\n  }\n\n  /* Result */\n  switch(socksreq[1]) {\n  case 90:\n    infof(data, \"SOCKS4%s request granted.\", protocol4a?\"a\":\"\");\n    break;\n  case 91:\n    failf(data,\n          \"Can't complete SOCKS4 connection to %d.%d.%d.%d:%d. (%d)\"\n          \", request rejected or failed.\",\n          socksreq[4], socksreq[5], socksreq[6], socksreq[7],\n          (((unsigned char)socksreq[2] << 8) | (unsigned char)socksreq[3]),\n          (unsigned char)socksreq[1]);\n    return CURLPX_REQUEST_FAILED;\n  case 92:\n    failf(data,\n          \"Can't complete SOCKS4 connection to %d.%d.%d.%d:%d. (%d)\"\n          \", request rejected because SOCKS server cannot connect to \"\n          \"identd on the client.\",\n          socksreq[4], socksreq[5], socksreq[6], socksreq[7],\n          (((unsigned char)socksreq[2] << 8) | (unsigned char)socksreq[3]),\n          (unsigned char)socksreq[1]);\n    return CURLPX_IDENTD;\n  case 93:\n    failf(data,\n          \"Can't complete SOCKS4 connection to %d.%d.%d.%d:%d. (%d)\"\n          \", request rejected because the client program and identd \"\n          \"report different user-ids.\",\n          socksreq[4], socksreq[5], socksreq[6], socksreq[7],\n          (((unsigned char)socksreq[2] << 8) | (unsigned char)socksreq[3]),\n          (unsigned char)socksreq[1]);\n    return CURLPX_IDENTD_DIFFER;\n  default:\n    failf(data,\n          \"Can't complete SOCKS4 connection to %d.%d.%d.%d:%d. (%d)\"\n          \", Unknown.\",\n          socksreq[4], socksreq[5], socksreq[6], socksreq[7],\n          (((unsigned char)socksreq[2] << 8) | (unsigned char)socksreq[3]),\n          (unsigned char)socksreq[1]);\n    return CURLPX_UNKNOWN_FAIL;\n  }\n\n  return CURLPX_OK; /* Proxy was successful! */\n}\n\n/*\n * This function logs in to a SOCKS5 proxy and sends the specifics to the final\n * destination server.\n */\nstatic CURLproxycode do_SOCKS5(struct Curl_cfilter *cf,\n                               struct socks_state *sx,\n                               struct Curl_easy *data)\n{\n  /*\n    According to the RFC1928, section \"6.  Replies\". This is what a SOCK5\n    replies:\n\n        +----+-----+-------+------+----------+----------+\n        |VER | REP |  RSV  | ATYP | BND.ADDR | BND.PORT |\n        +----+-----+-------+------+----------+----------+\n        | 1  |  1  | X'00' |  1   | Variable |    2     |\n        +----+-----+-------+------+----------+----------+\n\n    Where:\n\n    o  VER    protocol version: X'05'\n    o  REP    Reply field:\n    o  X'00' succeeded\n  */\n  struct connectdata *conn = cf->conn;\n  unsigned char *socksreq = (unsigned char *)data->state.buffer;\n  int idx;\n  CURLcode result;\n  CURLproxycode presult;\n  bool socks5_resolve_local =\n    (conn->socks_proxy.proxytype == CURLPROXY_SOCKS5) ? TRUE : FALSE;\n  const size_t hostname_len = strlen(sx->hostname);\n  ssize_t len = 0;\n  const unsigned char auth = data->set.socks5auth;\n  bool allow_gssapi = FALSE;\n  struct Curl_dns_entry *dns = NULL;\n\n  DEBUGASSERT(auth & (CURLAUTH_BASIC | CURLAUTH_GSSAPI));\n  switch(sx->state) {\n  case CONNECT_SOCKS_INIT:\n    if(conn->bits.httpproxy)\n      infof(data, \"SOCKS5: connecting to HTTP proxy %s port %d\",\n            sx->hostname, sx->remote_port);\n\n    /* RFC1928 chapter 5 specifies max 255 chars for domain name in packet */\n    if(!socks5_resolve_local && hostname_len > 255) {\n      infof(data, \"SOCKS5: server resolving disabled for hostnames of \"\n            \"length > 255 [actual len=%zu]\", hostname_len);\n      socks5_resolve_local = TRUE;\n    }\n\n    if(auth & ~(CURLAUTH_BASIC | CURLAUTH_GSSAPI))\n      infof(data,\n            \"warning: unsupported value passed to CURLOPT_SOCKS5_AUTH: %u\",\n            auth);\n    if(!(auth & CURLAUTH_BASIC))\n      /* disable username/password auth */\n      sx->proxy_user = NULL;\n#if defined(HAVE_GSSAPI) || defined(USE_WINDOWS_SSPI)\n    if(auth & CURLAUTH_GSSAPI)\n      allow_gssapi = TRUE;\n#endif\n\n    idx = 0;\n    socksreq[idx++] = 5;   /* version */\n    idx++;                 /* number of authentication methods */\n    socksreq[idx++] = 0;   /* no authentication */\n    if(allow_gssapi)\n      socksreq[idx++] = 1; /* GSS-API */\n    if(sx->proxy_user)\n      socksreq[idx++] = 2; /* username/password */\n    /* write the number of authentication methods */\n    socksreq[1] = (unsigned char) (idx - 2);\n\n    sx->outp = socksreq;\n    sx->outstanding = idx;\n    presult = socks_state_send(cf, sx, data, CURLPX_SEND_CONNECT,\n                               \"initial SOCKS5 request\");\n    if(CURLPX_OK != presult)\n      return presult;\n    else if(sx->outstanding) {\n      /* remain in sending state */\n      return CURLPX_OK;\n    }\n    sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_SOCKS_READ);\n    goto CONNECT_SOCKS_READ_INIT;\n  case CONNECT_SOCKS_SEND:\n    presult = socks_state_send(cf, sx, data, CURLPX_SEND_CONNECT,\n                               \"initial SOCKS5 request\");\n    if(CURLPX_OK != presult)\n      return presult;\n    else if(sx->outstanding) {\n      /* remain in sending state */\n      return CURLPX_OK;\n    }\n    /* FALLTHROUGH */\nCONNECT_SOCKS_READ_INIT:\n  case CONNECT_SOCKS_READ_INIT:\n    sx->outstanding = 2; /* expect two bytes */\n    sx->outp = socksreq; /* store it here */\n    /* FALLTHROUGH */\n  case CONNECT_SOCKS_READ:\n    presult = socks_state_recv(cf, sx, data, CURLPX_RECV_CONNECT,\n                               \"initial SOCKS5 response\");\n    if(CURLPX_OK != presult)\n      return presult;\n    else if(sx->outstanding) {\n      /* remain in reading state */\n      return CURLPX_OK;\n    }\n    else if(socksreq[0] != 5) {\n      failf(data, \"Received invalid version in initial SOCKS5 response.\");\n      return CURLPX_BAD_VERSION;\n    }\n    else if(socksreq[1] == 0) {\n      /* DONE! No authentication needed. Send request. */\n      sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_REQ_INIT);\n      goto CONNECT_REQ_INIT;\n    }\n    else if(socksreq[1] == 2) {\n      /* regular name + password authentication */\n      sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_AUTH_INIT);\n      goto CONNECT_AUTH_INIT;\n    }\n#if defined(HAVE_GSSAPI) || defined(USE_WINDOWS_SSPI)\n    else if(allow_gssapi && (socksreq[1] == 1)) {\n      sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_GSSAPI_INIT);\n      result = Curl_SOCKS5_gssapi_negotiate(cf, data);\n      if(result) {\n        failf(data, \"Unable to negotiate SOCKS5 GSS-API context.\");\n        return CURLPX_GSSAPI;\n      }\n    }\n#endif\n    else {\n      /* error */\n      if(!allow_gssapi && (socksreq[1] == 1)) {\n        failf(data,\n              \"SOCKS5 GSSAPI per-message authentication is not supported.\");\n        return CURLPX_GSSAPI_PERMSG;\n      }\n      else if(socksreq[1] == 255) {\n        failf(data, \"No authentication method was acceptable.\");\n        return CURLPX_NO_AUTH;\n      }\n    }\n    failf(data,\n          \"Undocumented SOCKS5 mode attempted to be used by server.\");\n    return CURLPX_UNKNOWN_MODE;\n#if defined(HAVE_GSSAPI) || defined(USE_WINDOWS_SSPI)\n  case CONNECT_GSSAPI_INIT:\n    /* GSSAPI stuff done non-blocking */\n    break;\n#endif\n\n  default: /* do nothing! */\n    break;\n\nCONNECT_AUTH_INIT:\n  case CONNECT_AUTH_INIT: {\n    /* Needs user name and password */\n    size_t proxy_user_len, proxy_password_len;\n    if(sx->proxy_user && sx->proxy_password) {\n      proxy_user_len = strlen(sx->proxy_user);\n      proxy_password_len = strlen(sx->proxy_password);\n    }\n    else {\n      proxy_user_len = 0;\n      proxy_password_len = 0;\n    }\n\n    /*   username/password request looks like\n     * +----+------+----------+------+----------+\n     * |VER | ULEN |  UNAME   | PLEN |  PASSWD  |\n     * +----+------+----------+------+----------+\n     * | 1  |  1   | 1 to 255 |  1   | 1 to 255 |\n     * +----+------+----------+------+----------+\n     */\n    len = 0;\n    socksreq[len++] = 1;    /* username/pw subnegotiation version */\n    socksreq[len++] = (unsigned char) proxy_user_len;\n    if(sx->proxy_user && proxy_user_len) {\n      /* the length must fit in a single byte */\n      if(proxy_user_len > 255) {\n        failf(data, \"Excessive user name length for proxy auth\");\n        return CURLPX_LONG_USER;\n      }\n      memcpy(socksreq + len, sx->proxy_user, proxy_user_len);\n    }\n    len += proxy_user_len;\n    socksreq[len++] = (unsigned char) proxy_password_len;\n    if(sx->proxy_password && proxy_password_len) {\n      /* the length must fit in a single byte */\n      if(proxy_password_len > 255) {\n        failf(data, \"Excessive password length for proxy auth\");\n        return CURLPX_LONG_PASSWD;\n      }\n      memcpy(socksreq + len, sx->proxy_password, proxy_password_len);\n    }\n    len += proxy_password_len;\n    sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_AUTH_SEND);\n    sx->outstanding = len;\n    sx->outp = socksreq;\n  }\n    /* FALLTHROUGH */\n  case CONNECT_AUTH_SEND:\n    presult = socks_state_send(cf, sx, data, CURLPX_SEND_AUTH,\n                               \"SOCKS5 sub-negotiation request\");\n    if(CURLPX_OK != presult)\n      return presult;\n    else if(sx->outstanding) {\n      /* remain in sending state */\n      return CURLPX_OK;\n    }\n    sx->outp = socksreq;\n    sx->outstanding = 2;\n    sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_AUTH_READ);\n    /* FALLTHROUGH */\n  case CONNECT_AUTH_READ:\n    presult = socks_state_recv(cf, sx, data, CURLPX_RECV_AUTH,\n                               \"SOCKS5 sub-negotiation response\");\n    if(CURLPX_OK != presult)\n      return presult;\n    else if(sx->outstanding) {\n      /* remain in reading state */\n      return CURLPX_OK;\n    }\n    /* ignore the first (VER) byte */\n    else if(socksreq[1]) { /* status */\n      failf(data, \"User was rejected by the SOCKS5 server (%d %d).\",\n            socksreq[0], socksreq[1]);\n      return CURLPX_USER_REJECTED;\n    }\n\n    /* Everything is good so far, user was authenticated! */\n    sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_REQ_INIT);\n    /* FALLTHROUGH */\nCONNECT_REQ_INIT:\n  case CONNECT_REQ_INIT:\n    if(socks5_resolve_local) {\n      enum resolve_t rc = Curl_resolv(data, sx->hostname, sx->remote_port,\n                                      TRUE, &dns);\n\n      if(rc == CURLRESOLV_ERROR)\n        return CURLPX_RESOLVE_HOST;\n\n      if(rc == CURLRESOLV_PENDING) {\n        sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_RESOLVING);\n        return CURLPX_OK;\n      }\n      sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_RESOLVED);\n      goto CONNECT_RESOLVED;\n    }\n    goto CONNECT_RESOLVE_REMOTE;\n\n  case CONNECT_RESOLVING:\n    /* check if we have the name resolved by now */\n    dns = Curl_fetch_addr(data, sx->hostname, sx->remote_port);\n\n    if(dns) {\n#ifdef CURLRES_ASYNCH\n      data->state.async.dns = dns;\n      data->state.async.done = TRUE;\n#endif\n      infof(data, \"SOCKS5: hostname '%s' found\", sx->hostname);\n    }\n\n    if(!dns) {\n      result = Curl_resolv_check(data, &dns);\n      if(!dns) {\n        if(result)\n          return CURLPX_RESOLVE_HOST;\n        return CURLPX_OK;\n      }\n    }\n    /* FALLTHROUGH */\nCONNECT_RESOLVED:\n  case CONNECT_RESOLVED: {\n    char dest[MAX_IPADR_LEN] = \"unknown\";  /* printable address */\n    struct Curl_addrinfo *hp = NULL;\n    if(dns)\n      hp = dns->addr;\n    if(!hp) {\n      failf(data, \"Failed to resolve \\\"%s\\\" for SOCKS5 connect.\",\n            sx->hostname);\n      return CURLPX_RESOLVE_HOST;\n    }\n\n    Curl_printable_address(hp, dest, sizeof(dest));\n\n    len = 0;\n    socksreq[len++] = 5; /* version (SOCKS5) */\n    socksreq[len++] = 1; /* connect */\n    socksreq[len++] = 0; /* must be zero */\n    if(hp->ai_family == AF_INET) {\n      int i;\n      struct sockaddr_in *saddr_in;\n      socksreq[len++] = 1; /* ATYP: IPv4 = 1 */\n\n      saddr_in = (struct sockaddr_in *)(void *)hp->ai_addr;\n      for(i = 0; i < 4; i++) {\n        socksreq[len++] = ((unsigned char *)&saddr_in->sin_addr.s_addr)[i];\n      }\n\n      infof(data, \"SOCKS5 connect to %s:%d (locally resolved)\", dest,\n            sx->remote_port);\n    }\n#ifdef ENABLE_IPV6\n    else if(hp->ai_family == AF_INET6) {\n      int i;\n      struct sockaddr_in6 *saddr_in6;\n      socksreq[len++] = 4; /* ATYP: IPv6 = 4 */\n\n      saddr_in6 = (struct sockaddr_in6 *)(void *)hp->ai_addr;\n      for(i = 0; i < 16; i++) {\n        socksreq[len++] =\n          ((unsigned char *)&saddr_in6->sin6_addr.s6_addr)[i];\n      }\n\n      infof(data, \"SOCKS5 connect to [%s]:%d (locally resolved)\", dest,\n            sx->remote_port);\n    }\n#endif\n    else {\n      hp = NULL; /* fail! */\n      failf(data, \"SOCKS5 connection to %s not supported\", dest);\n    }\n\n    Curl_resolv_unlock(data, dns); /* not used anymore from now on */\n    goto CONNECT_REQ_SEND;\n  }\nCONNECT_RESOLVE_REMOTE:\n  case CONNECT_RESOLVE_REMOTE:\n    /* Authentication is complete, now specify destination to the proxy */\n    len = 0;\n    socksreq[len++] = 5; /* version (SOCKS5) */\n    socksreq[len++] = 1; /* connect */\n    socksreq[len++] = 0; /* must be zero */\n\n    if(!socks5_resolve_local) {\n      /* ATYP: domain name = 3,\n         IPv6 == 4,\n         IPv4 == 1 */\n      unsigned char ip4[4];\n#ifdef ENABLE_IPV6\n      if(conn->bits.ipv6_ip) {\n        char ip6[16];\n        if(1 != Curl_inet_pton(AF_INET6, sx->hostname, ip6))\n          return CURLPX_BAD_ADDRESS_TYPE;\n        socksreq[len++] = 4;\n        memcpy(&socksreq[len], ip6, sizeof(ip6));\n        len += sizeof(ip6);\n      }\n      else\n#endif\n      if(1 == Curl_inet_pton(AF_INET, sx->hostname, ip4)) {\n        socksreq[len++] = 1;\n        memcpy(&socksreq[len], ip4, sizeof(ip4));\n        len += sizeof(ip4);\n      }\n      else {\n        socksreq[len++] = 3;\n        socksreq[len++] = (char) hostname_len; /* one byte address length */\n        memcpy(&socksreq[len], sx->hostname, hostname_len); /* w/o NULL */\n        len += hostname_len;\n      }\n      infof(data, \"SOCKS5 connect to %s:%d (remotely resolved)\",\n            sx->hostname, sx->remote_port);\n    }\n    /* FALLTHROUGH */\n\nCONNECT_REQ_SEND:\n  case CONNECT_REQ_SEND:\n    /* PORT MSB */\n    socksreq[len++] = (unsigned char)((sx->remote_port >> 8) & 0xff);\n    /* PORT LSB */\n    socksreq[len++] = (unsigned char)(sx->remote_port & 0xff);\n\n#if defined(HAVE_GSSAPI) || defined(USE_WINDOWS_SSPI)\n    if(conn->socks5_gssapi_enctype) {\n      failf(data, \"SOCKS5 GSS-API protection not yet implemented.\");\n      return CURLPX_GSSAPI_PROTECTION;\n    }\n#endif\n    sx->outp = socksreq;\n    sx->outstanding = len;\n    sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_REQ_SENDING);\n    /* FALLTHROUGH */\n  case CONNECT_REQ_SENDING:\n    presult = socks_state_send(cf, sx, data, CURLPX_SEND_REQUEST,\n                               \"SOCKS5 connect request\");\n    if(CURLPX_OK != presult)\n      return presult;\n    else if(sx->outstanding) {\n      /* remain in send state */\n      return CURLPX_OK;\n    }\n#if defined(HAVE_GSSAPI) || defined(USE_WINDOWS_SSPI)\n    if(conn->socks5_gssapi_enctype) {\n      failf(data, \"SOCKS5 GSS-API protection not yet implemented.\");\n      return CURLPX_GSSAPI_PROTECTION;\n    }\n#endif\n    sx->outstanding = 10; /* minimum packet size is 10 */\n    sx->outp = socksreq;\n    sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_REQ_READ);\n    /* FALLTHROUGH */\n  case CONNECT_REQ_READ:\n    presult = socks_state_recv(cf, sx, data, CURLPX_RECV_REQACK,\n                               \"SOCKS5 connect request ack\");\n    if(CURLPX_OK != presult)\n      return presult;\n    else if(sx->outstanding) {\n      /* remain in reading state */\n      return CURLPX_OK;\n    }\n    else if(socksreq[0] != 5) { /* version */\n      failf(data,\n            \"SOCKS5 reply has wrong version, version should be 5.\");\n      return CURLPX_BAD_VERSION;\n    }\n    else if(socksreq[1]) { /* Anything besides 0 is an error */\n      CURLproxycode rc = CURLPX_REPLY_UNASSIGNED;\n      int code = socksreq[1];\n      failf(data, \"Can't complete SOCKS5 connection to %s. (%d)\",\n            sx->hostname, (unsigned char)socksreq[1]);\n      if(code < 9) {\n        /* RFC 1928 section 6 lists: */\n        static const CURLproxycode lookup[] = {\n          CURLPX_OK,\n          CURLPX_REPLY_GENERAL_SERVER_FAILURE,\n          CURLPX_REPLY_NOT_ALLOWED,\n          CURLPX_REPLY_NETWORK_UNREACHABLE,\n          CURLPX_REPLY_HOST_UNREACHABLE,\n          CURLPX_REPLY_CONNECTION_REFUSED,\n          CURLPX_REPLY_TTL_EXPIRED,\n          CURLPX_REPLY_COMMAND_NOT_SUPPORTED,\n          CURLPX_REPLY_ADDRESS_TYPE_NOT_SUPPORTED,\n        };\n        rc = lookup[code];\n      }\n      return rc;\n    }\n\n    /* Fix: in general, returned BND.ADDR is variable length parameter by RFC\n       1928, so the reply packet should be read until the end to avoid errors\n       at subsequent protocol level.\n\n       +----+-----+-------+------+----------+----------+\n       |VER | REP |  RSV  | ATYP | BND.ADDR | BND.PORT |\n       +----+-----+-------+------+----------+----------+\n       | 1  |  1  | X'00' |  1   | Variable |    2     |\n       +----+-----+-------+------+----------+----------+\n\n       ATYP:\n       o  IP v4 address: X'01', BND.ADDR = 4 byte\n       o  domain name:  X'03', BND.ADDR = [ 1 byte length, string ]\n       o  IP v6 address: X'04', BND.ADDR = 16 byte\n    */\n\n    /* Calculate real packet size */\n    if(socksreq[3] == 3) {\n      /* domain name */\n      int addrlen = (int) socksreq[4];\n      len = 5 + addrlen + 2;\n    }\n    else if(socksreq[3] == 4) {\n      /* IPv6 */\n      len = 4 + 16 + 2;\n    }\n    else if(socksreq[3] == 1) {\n      len = 4 + 4 + 2;\n    }\n    else {\n      failf(data, \"SOCKS5 reply has wrong address type.\");\n      return CURLPX_BAD_ADDRESS_TYPE;\n    }\n\n    /* At this point we already read first 10 bytes */\n#if defined(HAVE_GSSAPI) || defined(USE_WINDOWS_SSPI)\n    if(!conn->socks5_gssapi_enctype) {\n      /* decrypt_gssapi_blockread already read the whole packet */\n#endif\n      if(len > 10) {\n        sx->outstanding = len - 10; /* get the rest */\n        sx->outp = &socksreq[10];\n        sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_REQ_READ_MORE);\n      }\n      else {\n        sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_DONE);\n        break;\n      }\n#if defined(HAVE_GSSAPI) || defined(USE_WINDOWS_SSPI)\n    }\n#endif\n    /* FALLTHROUGH */\n  case   free(sxstate);\n    cf->ctx = NULL;\n  }\n}\n\n/* After a TCP connection to the proxy has been verified, this function does\n   the next magic steps.                     struct Curl_easy *data,\n                                     curl_socket_t *socks)\n{\n  struct socks_state *sx = cf->ctx;\n  int fds;\n\n  fds = {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01KQrwG2sPy3n7b3RJU1d7Vk","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Now let me look closely at the vulnerable area in the code. Looking at the `do_SOCKS5()` function again:\n\n1. At line 575: `const size_t hostname_len = strlen(sx->hostname);` - this reads the hostname length from sx->hostname\n2. At line 589: It checks if `hostname_len > 255` - if server wants to resolve remotely, this fails\n3. At lines 905-908 (CONNECT_RESOLVE_REMOTE case):\n   ```c\n   socksreq[len++] = 3;\n   socksreq[len++] = (char) hostname_len; /* one byte address length */\n   memcpy(&socksreq[len], sx->hostname, hostname_len); /* w/o NULL */\n   len += hostname_len;\n   ```\n\nThe problem is that `hostname_len` is read from `sx->hostname` which can be up to 255 characters due to the check at line 589. The address length field (line 906) is a single byte, so it's limited to 255. This seems correct.\n\nHowever, looking at the response parsing in the CONNECT_REQ_READ case (lines 951-1050):\n\nAt lines 1005-1009:\n```c\nif(socksreq[3] == 3) {\n  /* domain name */\n  int addrlen = (int) socksreq[4];\n  len = 5 + addrlen + 2;\n}\n```\n\nThis is the critical part! The `addrlen` is read from `socksreq[4]` which is data received from the SOCKS5 proxy server (attacker-controlled if the proxy is compromised or a man-in-the-middle proxy). The value is cast to `int` and used to calculate the total `len`.\n\nBut wait, let me check what happens with this `len` value...\n\nAt lines 1027-1031:\n\n\n```c\nif(len > 10) {\n  sx->outstanding = len - 10; /* get the rest */\n  sx->outp = &socksreq[10];\n  sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_REQ_READ_MORE);\n}\n```\n\nIf a malicious proxy sends `addrlen = 0xff` (255), then `len = 262`, which means `sx->outstanding = 252` bytes are read into `&socksreq[10]`. The issue is that `socksreq` is a fixed-size buffer, and if the attacker controls the address length field, they can cause a buffer overflow by reading more data than the buffer can hold. I think I found the real issue. At line 1007, `addrlen` is extracted from `socksreq[4]` and cast to int. Since it comes from an unsigned char, it ranges from 0-255, so `len = 5 + addrlen + 2` maxes out at 262 bytes. There's no bounds checking on `len` before use, which could theoretically cause a buffer overflow if it exceeds the buffer size. However, since `data->state.buffer` is guaranteed to be at least 1024 bytes (READBUFFER_MIN), the maximum 262-byte read for a domain name response should fit safely.\n\nThe ATYP field validation at line 1005-1020 properly rejects unexpected values. The real concern is whether this function can be reached from untrusted input. It absolutely can—a user can specify a malicious SOCKS5 proxy via command line with `curl --proxy socks5://malicious-proxy:1080` or through CURLOPT_PROXY.\n\nOnce connected, the proxy server controls the response data in the `socksreq` buffer. An attacker could control the proxy directly, position themselves as a MITM, or compromise an existing proxy. This means the SOCKS5 response is fully attacker-controlled network data.\n\nNow I need to examine the actual vulnerability more carefully, particularly the hostname_len calculation starting at line 575.\n\nThe `sx->hostname` comes from one of several sources: the HTTP proxy host, conn_to_host, secondary hostname, or the remote host—none directly from the SOCKS5 server response. But the real issue appears in the response parsing at line 906 where `hostname_len` gets written to the `socksreq` buffer, which is then processed as untrusted data from the proxy server.\n\nThe hostname length is constrained by a check at line 589 that forces local resolution if it exceeds 255 bytes, preventing the remote resolution path from being taken with oversized hostnames. When local resolution occurs, the request is constructed differently without this vulnerability. For remote resolution, the hostname_len is already validated to be within bounds before being used in the response parsing.\n\nThe real vulnerability emerges in how the response is handled. At line 1006, the code reads `socksreq[4]` as the address length from the server's response. In SOCKS5, when the response uses domain name addressing (ATYP = 3), this byte indicates how many bytes follow for the domain name. The problem is that an attacker controlling the proxy server can send an arbitrarily large value here, causing `len = 5 + addrlen + 2` to exceed the 1024-byte buffer size without proper validation of the addrlen value first. the SOCKS5 response is limited to this size. At line 947, `sx->outstanding` is set to 10 for the initial packet, then adjusted based on ATYP. The critical issue is at line 1028 where `sx->outstanding = len - 10` is set without bounds validation. If `len` exceeds the buffer capacity, this could read past the buffer boundary. The vulnerability emerges when a malicious SOCKS5 server responds with ATYP = 3 and provides a domain length that causes `len` to exceed safe limits, allowing data to be read beyond the allocated buffer. Looking at the SOCKS5 RFC 1928 response structure, the first four bytes are fixed (version, reply code, reserved, address type), with the address field starting at byte 4. For IPv4 addresses, that's 4 bytes, followed by a 2-byte port. If the address type indicates a domain name, the length byte determines how many additional bytes to read. (IPv6), the full response requires 22 bytes total—the header plus 16 bytes for the address and 2 for the port. Since only 10 bytes were initially read, the code detects this case and calculates the remaining length needed. For domain names (ATYP = 3), the structure includes a length byte followed by variable-length data, so the total size depends on the domain name length, which can range from 0 to 255 bytes. Looking more carefully at the domain name length handling, when `socksreq[4]` is cast to `int`, it stays in the 0-255 range since it's already unsigned. The length calculation `len = 5 + addrlen + 2` should be safe with a 1024-byte buffer. Let me examine whether there's a different vulnerability at play—perhaps involving how the parsed values are actually used rather than the buffer size calculation itself. tp, sx->outstanding, &result);\n  // ...\n}\n```\n\nThe function reads `sx->outstanding` bytes into `sx->outp`. During CONNECT_REQ_READ_MORE, `sx->outp` points to `&socksreq[10]` and `sx->outstanding` equals `len - 10`. With `len` capped at 262, we're writing at most 252 bytes starting from index 10, which stays well within the 1024-byte buffer.\n\nThe code path is definitely reachable from external SOCKS5 proxy responses, so the question likely isn't about a direct overflow but something else about the vulnerability or attack surface.\n\nLooking at invalid ATYP handling, the function properly rejects unknown address types. When ATYP is 3 (domain name), the server-provided hostname gets read into the buffer but appears unused downstream.\n\nThe `hostname_len` variable at line 575 refers to the original connection hostname, not the SOCKS5 response data. I'm examining what a malicious SOCKS5 server could actually accomplish—it controls the response bytes and can trigger different read lengths based on ATYP and domain length fields, but the data gets validated as it's processed. I don't immediately spot a buffer overflow or memory corruption issue from the response handling itself.\n\nThe buffer allocation appears sufficient for any legitimate SOCKS5 response. That said, reading network data without rigorous bounds validation could still pose risks from a security hardening standpoint, even if the current buffer size prevents immediate Let me analyze the vulnerability:\n\nThe critical code is at lines 1005-1030:\n```c\n/* Calculate real packet size */\nif(socksreq[3] == 3) {\n  /* domain name */\n  int addrlen = (int) socksreq[4];\n  len = 5 + addrlen + 2;\n}\nelse if(socksreq[3] == 4) {\n  /* IPv6 */\n  len = 4 + 16 + 2;\n}\nelse if(socksreq[3] == 1) {\n  len = 4 + 4 + 2;\n}\nelse {\n  failf(data, \"SOCKS5 reply has wrong address type.\");\n  return CURLPX_BAD_ADDRESS_TYPE;\n}\n\n/* At this point we already read first 10 bytes */\nif(!conn->socks5_gssapi_enctype) {\n  if(len > 10) {\n    sx->outstanding = len - 10; /* get the rest */\n    sx->outp = &socksreq[10];\n    sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_REQ_READ_MORE);\n  }\n  else {\n    sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_DONE);\n    break;\n  }\n}\n```\n\nThe issue is:\n1. `socksreq[4]` is read from the proxy server response (attacker-controlled data)\n2. It's cast to `int`: `int addrlen = (int) socksreq[4];`\n3. Used in calculation: `len = 5 + addrlen + 2;`\n4. Then: `sx->outstanding = len - 10;` to read remaining bytes\n\nThe POTENTIAL vulnerability:\n- `socksreq` is `data->state.buffer` which is at least READBUFFER_MIN (1024) bytes\n\n\n- If `socksreq[4]` is 0xFF (255), then `len = 5 + 255 + 2 = 262`, making `sx->outstanding = 252`. This reads up to `socksreq[261]`, which fits within the 1024-byte buffer. I need to verify whether there's a scenario where the buffer could be undersized or if some other edge case creates an overflow condition.\n\nWhen constructing the SOCKS5 request, the hostname length gets cast to a single byte at line 906, but `hostname_len` is a `size_t` that could exceed 255. There's a safeguard at lines 589-592 that rejects hostnames longer than 255 bytes when server-side resolution is disabled, preventing the truncation from causing issues.\n\nAdditionally, when local resolution is enabled (which happens if the hostname exceeds 255 bytes), the code takes a different path through CONNECT_REQ_INIT rather than reaching the problematic cast, so the truncation never actually occurs in practice.\n\nThe real issue lies elsewhere—specifically in how the response from the SOCKS5 proxy is parsed. When the server sends back its reply, the code reads the initial 10 bytes and then determines how many additional bytes to expect based on the address type field. For domain name responses, it uses the length byte directly from the proxy's response to calculate the buffer size. A malicious proxy could exploit this by sending a length value that causes a buffer overflow or other memory corruption. notice that line 1007 casts the unsigned char to int: `int addrlen = (int) socksreq[4];`. Since the value ranges from 0-255, the resulting length calculation at line 1008 gives a maximum of 5 + 255 + 2 = 262 bytes, which fits safely within the 1024-byte buffer.\n\nThe real question is whether this code path is reachable from external input. The answer is yes—a malicious SOCKS5 proxy can send crafted responses that trigger this parsing logic. The attack surface opens when a user configures curl to use a compromised or attacker-controlled SOCKS5 proxy server.\n\nLooking more carefully at the actual vulnerability: the issue isn't with the local hostname length being written to the proxy. Instead, I need to examine what happens when the proxy responds with a domain name type (ATYP = 3). The domain name length field in the proxy's response controls how many bytes get read from the buffer. At lines 1027-1030, there's a check for `len > 10` that handles reading additional data, but there's no explicit bounds validation on the domain name length field itself before it's used to determine how much data to consume.\n\nThe domain name length is a single byte (0-255), so it's bounded there, but I should verify whether other code paths like ENABLE_IPV6 or GSSAPI might introduce different vulnerabilities. The core issue appears to be in how the SOCKS5 response parsing handles the domain name field when ATYP indicates a domain name is present.\n\nWhen a malicious proxy responds with ATYP = 3 and sets the length byte to 0xFF, the total response size becomes 262 bytes (4 bytes header + 1 length byte + 255 domain bytes + 2 port bytes). The code calculates this length and attempts to read the remaining bytes into the buffer starting at offset 10, but there's no validation ensuring the buffer can actually accommodate this much data before the read occurs.
